Main Question\n\nThe project asks one main question.\n\n`Can metacognitive control learned at test time improve OOD problem solving by changing behavior, not just style?`\n\nWe answer it through three research questions.\n\n1. `RQ1: Meta-CoT`\n   - Can the model emit parseable metacognitive state that is cleanly separated from ordinary CoT?\n2. `RQ2: Meta-RL`\n   - Can that metacognitive state be turned into verifiable reward signals and learned as a control policy?\n3. `RQ3: Curriculum`\n   - Can the same metacognitive state trigger diagnosis, retrieval, and adaptation for open-ended recovery?\n\n## 2. Project Intent\n\n### 2.1 Intent A: Meta-CoT must be a controller, not decorative self-talk\n\nWe do not want longer answers or generic reflection.\n\n1. `confidence` must be a control variable that changes with risk.\n2. `something feels off` or meaningful confidence drop must trigger redirect behavior.\n3. `confidence remains high but support is weak` must trigger verify behavior.\n4. `diagnosis` must explain why the current route is weak.\n5. `study_need` must expose what skill, perspective, or object of study is missing.\n6. meta blocks must stay strictly separate from ordinary derivation.\n\nMeta blocks therefore carry only:\n\n1. local confidence\n2. anomaly / conflict notice\n3. failure diagnosis\n4. next control action\n5. optional `study_need`\n\nMeta blocks should not contain ordinary algebraic derivation or full CoT.\n\n### 2.2 Intent B: Meta-RL must make those behaviors verifiable\n\nThe RL stage is not “optimize everything at once”.\n\n1. first improve calibration\n2. then improve confidence revision around intervention points\n3. then test isolated behavior rewards one by one\n4. only then run the combined controller\n\nThe decomposition exists to answer causal questions, not only to get a better final number.\n\n### 2.3 Intent C: Curriculum must start from diagnosis\n\nCurriculum and RAG are only meaningful if the model can say:\n\n1. why the current attempt is failing\n2. what missing knowledge or perspective is needed next\n3. whether retrieval or one-example adaptation is actually justified\n\nThe long-term target is:\n\n`diagnose -> expose study_need -> retrieve/adapt -> retry`\n\n## 3. Intent / Hypothesis / Verification\n\n### 3.1 RQ1: Meta-CoT\n\n`Intent`\n\n1. teach pure metacognitive control state\n2. keep meta separate from derivation\n3. test whether the learned state actually enables test-time adaptation on hard and OOD problems\n\n`Hypotheses`\n\n1. `H1a`\n   - `V2/V3/V5 SFT` can teach parseable confidence and meta tags without collapsing math ability.\n2. `H1b`\n   - the learned meta traces will express controller state rather than decorative chain-of-thought, and will causally precede verify / redirect / diagnosis actions.\n3. `H1c`\n   - diagnosis and `study_need` can be made parseable enough for later curriculum use.\n4. `H1d`\n   - the same meta state can improve retry-time adaptation on hard slices without large regression on base accuracy.\n\n`Verification`\n\n1. meta parse rate\n2. confidence extraction rate\n3. meta purity\n   - meta text contains diagnosis / control state / next action\n   - meta text does not contain ordinary derivation\n4. adaptation precursor coverage on hard problems\n5. adaptation lift\n   - `first_completion -> retry/intervention completion` delta on hard slices\n   - contrast between samples with versus without verify / redirect signals\n6. accuracy retention\n7. qualitative samples on hard problems, especially AIME-like failures\n\n### 3.2 RQ2: Meta-RL\n\n`Intent`\n\n1. learn better confidence calibration\n2. learn intervention-local confidence revision\n3. separate verify / redirect / diagnosis effects\n4. test whether those effects combine into a real controller\n\n`Hypotheses`\n\n1. `H2a`\n   - `E3` improves calibration even before explicit behavior rewards.\n2. `H2b`\n   - `E5` improves confidence revision around conflict or anomaly.\n3. `H2c`\n   - `E8` suppresses hard-slice overconfidence better than `E5`.\n4. `H2d`\n   - `E9 / E9b / E9c` isolate verify / redirect / diagnosis effects in interpretable ways.\n5. `H2e`\n   - `E10` combines those behavior rewards into a stronger controller than any single isolated policy.\n6. `H2f`\n   - `E6 / E7` are only meaningful if the probe estimates `p(correct | prefix)` rather than single-trajectory final correctness.\n\n`Verification`\n\n1. benchmark accuracy\n2. ECE / Brier / wrong-answer mean confidence / wrong high-confidence rate\n3. conflict-conditioned confidence drop\n4. verify precision under high confidence\n5. redirect-conditioned strategy-switch and recovery\n6. diagnosis consistency and usefulness\n7. repeated intervention quality on hard problems\n8. qualitative response analysis, not only reward averages\n\n### 3.3 RQ3: Curriculum\n\n`Intent`\n\n1. make diagnosis actionable\n2. expose `study_need` as a parseable retrieval trigger\n3. connect failure analysis to no-training RAG or one-example adaptation\n\n`Hypotheses`\n\n1. `H3a`\n   - decorative low confidence alone should not trigger retrieval.\n2. `H3b`\n   - diagnosis plus `study_need` should trigger retrieval much more precisely.\n3. `H3c`\n   - retrieved examples or one-example adaptation should improve retry accuracy only when diagnosis is meaningful.\n\n`Verification`\n\n1. retrieval trigger precision\n2. diagnosis / `study_need` coverage\n3. retry prompt artifact logging\n4. retry accuracy delta\n5. reproducible saved outputs for later audit\n\n## 4. Experiment Matrix\n\n| Experiment | Intent | Hypothesis | Verification |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| `V2 / V3 / V5 SFT` | establish parseable meta representation | H1a, H1b, H1c | parseability, purity, confidence extraction, accuracy retention |\n| `control_v5_verify_sft` | isolated verify controller | verify can be taught without redirect | high-confidence verify precision |\n| `control_v5_redirect_sft` | isolated redirect controller | redirect can be taught without verify | redirect recovery and strategy switch |\n| `control_v5_all_sft` | unified controller SFT | verify, redirect, diagnosis can coexist | unified behavior with limited accuracy loss |\n| `E3` | pure calibration | H2a | ECE, Brier, wrong high-confidence rate |\n| `E5` | calibration + confidence revision | H2b | conflict-conditioned confidence drop, no-drop wrong-commit |\n| `E6` | probe calibration | H2f | `|confidence - p_hat_probe|`, probe-aligned ECE |\n| `E7` | probe + blockwise stepwise | H2f | block-level probe gap, intervention-local calibration |\n| `E8` | stronger anti-overconfidence shaping | H2c | hard-slice calibration, wrong-high-confidence suppression |\n| `E9` | verify-only decomposition | H2d | verify precision, verify-conditioned error |\n| `E9b` | redirect-only decomposition | H2d | redirect recovery, real switch fraction |\n| `E9c` | diagnosis-only decomposition | H2d | diagnosis consistency, `study_need` usefulness |\n| `E10` | full combined controller | H2e | verify + redirect + diagnosis closure |\n| `Curriculum / RAG` | weakness-conditioned retrieval/adaptation | H3a, H3b, H3c | trigger precision, retry gain, study_need quality |\n\n## 5. {"type":"item.completed","item":{"id":"item_3","type":"command_execution","command":"/bin/bash -lc \"sed -n '1,260p' results/experiment_plan_v5.md\"","aggregated_output":"# Meta-CoT Experiment Plan v5: Fixing Meta Execution\n\n**Date**: 2026-04-04\n**Author**: Seungpil Lee\n**Project**: metacognition-math (Qwen3-8B)\n**Predecessor**: experiment_plan_v4.md (accuracy-focused autoresearch loop)\n\n---\n\n## 1. Current State Summary\n\n### What works\n\n1. **Parseable meta**: The SFT-trained model emits well-formed `<|meta|>...<|/meta|>` blocks containing confidence, diagnosis, and strategy statements. Coverage reaches 88.9% on `all_sft`.\n2. **Calibration (ECE reduction)**: E8 achieves ECE 0.322 with only 3.6% wrong-high-confidence, the best overconfidence suppression among all conditions.\n3. **Overconfidence suppression (E8)**: `overconfidence_penalty_reward` + `confidence_revision_reward` successfully pushed wrong-high-conf from 80.7% (verify_sft) down to 3.6% (E8).\n4. **Accuracy near parity (E9)**: E9 reaches 41.1% overall (base SFT: 42.2%), the closest Meta-CoT model to parity, driven by GSM8K 90.0%.\n\n### What does not work\n\n1. **Verify execution**: Verification is same-route repetition, not independent falsification. 15/53 wrong answers in E9 are overconfident-verify-failed: the model says \"verify\" then re-derives the same wrong answer (e.g., AIME 540 re-uses identical extremal intuition; GSM8K restart miscounts time identically).\n2. **Redirect execution**: Diagnosis appears but the solve body continues the original route. 0/4 diagnosis cases in E10 led to actual recovery. `effective_redirection_reward` checks `bool(solve_tail.strip())` for recovery, so any non-empty tail passes regardless of whether it contains a route switch.\n3. **Repeated intervention**: Hard problems get exactly one meta block. No ongoing controller loop is observed. The model treats meta as a one-shot annotation rather than an iterative self-monitor.\n4. **Full controller (E10)**: Only 5.6% confidence coverage. 53 out of 58 wrong answers have no meta signal at all. The model learned to omit confidence to avoid calibration penalties.\n\n### Quantitative reference (n=90 pilot, 30 per benchmark)\n\n| Model | Acc | AIME | GSM8K | MATH500 | conf_cov | ECE | wrong_high_conf |\n|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|\n| base_sft | 42.2 | 13.3 | 80.0 | 33.3 | 0.0 | n/a | n/a |\n| all_sft | 33.3 | 6.7 | 63.3 | 30.0 | 88.9 | 0.398 | 51.7 |\n| E8 | 38.9 | 10.0 | 80.0 | 26.7 | 23.3 | 0.322 | 3.6 |\n| E9 | 41.1 | 6.7 | 90.0 | 26.7 | 91.1 | 0.301 | 50.9 |\n| E9b | 40.0 | 6.7 | 83.3 | 30.0 | 0.0 | n/a | n/a |\n| E10 | 35.6 | 6.7 | 66.7 | 33.3 | 5.6 | 0.340 | 0.0 |\n\n---\n\n## 2. Root Cause Analysis\n\nThree code-level root causes explain why meta detection succeeds but meta execution fails.\n\n### Root Cause 1: `effective_verification_reward` rewards same-route repetition\n\n**Location**: `rewards.py` line 1016-1035, specifically `_has_effective_verification_signal` (line 119-125).\n\nThe function checks for word patterns (\"substitute\", \"plug back\", \"recalculat\") in the solve tail after the last meta block. The problem is that restating the same derivation with verification keywords counts as effective verification. There is no check for **structural independence** -- whether the verification method differs from the original solve route.\n\n**Consequence**: The model learns to append \"let me substitute back...\" followed by the same calculation. This gets rewarded at +0.8 for correct answers, reinforcing decorative verification.\n\n### Root Cause 2: `effective_redirection_reward` accepts any non-empty tail as recovery\n\n**Location**: `rewards.py` line 1038-1063, specifically line 1051: `has_tail_recovery = bool(solve_tail.strip())`.\n\nThe maximum reward (+1.0 for correct, +0.2 for wrong) requires `has_conflict and has_switch and has_drop and has_tail_recovery`. But `has_tail_recovery` is satisfied by any non-empty text after the last meta block -- including the original solve continuation that ignores the announced strategy switch.\n\n**Consequence**: The model announces \"switch to parity-based analysis\" in meta, then continues the original algebraic approach. Because the tail is non-empty, the redirection reward fires as if recovery occurred.\n\n### Root Cause 3: `calibration_reward` returns 0.0 for no meta, making omission cost-free\n\n**Location**: `rewards.py` line 656-710, specifically lines 679-680:\n\n```python\nif not blocks or all(b[\"confidence\"] is None for b in blocks):\n    rewards.append(0.0)\n```\n\nWhen the model emits no meta blocks or omits confidence, it receives 0.0 from calibration. Meanwhile, emitting confidence on wrong answers risks negative reward from both the Brier component and the log scoring rule. Rational reward optimization therefore favors omitting confidence entirely.\n\n**Consequence**: E5 (conf_cov=1.1%), E9b (conf_cov=0.0%), and E10 (conf_cov=5.6%) all escaped calibration pressure by reducing meta emission. This makes calibration metrics uninterpretable and defeats the purpose of Meta-CoT.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Proposed Experiments\n\nAll three experiments start from the same SFT checkpoint: `qwen3_metacot_control_v5_all_sft`. This ensures the only variable is the reward composition.\n\n### E9v2: Verify Quality\n\n**Node**: EVAL (GPU 0-3, same as current eval lane)\n\n**Intent**: Teach the model that verification must use an independent method, not repeat the same calculation. The current verify reward conflates \"mentions verification keywords\" with \"actually performs a structurally different check.\"\n\n**Hypothesis**: Adding `same_route_repetition_penalty` (-0.5 when the solve tail after a verify announcement shares >70% n-gram overlap with the pre-meta solve body) will reduce `overconfident_verify_failed` rate from 15/53 (28.3%, E9) to <5/53 (9.4%) without reducing overall accuracy by more than 2 percentage points.\n\n**Mechanism**: The new penalty computes character trigram overlap between the pre-meta solve prefix and the post-meta solve tail. If overlap exceeds 70%, the verification is classified as same-route repetition. The existing `effective_verification_reward` remains unchanged -- the penalty is additive, creating a gradient between \"verify with a new method (+0.8)\" and \"verify by restating (-0.5).\"\n\n**Verification**:\n- **Primary metric**: `overconfident_verify_failed` count on 1,030-problem eval. Target: <10% of wrong answers (currently 28.3%).\n- **Secondary metric**: `independent_method_rate` = fraction of verify completions where trigram overlap <70%. Target: >50%.\n- **Falsification condition**: If `wrong_high_conf` stays >40% despite the penalty, the trigram heuristic is too weak to detect repetition and a stronger structural check (e.g., operation-type extraction) is needed.\n\n**Reward composition**:\n\n| Reward function | Weight | Source |\n|---|---|---|\n| correctness_reward | 3.0 | E9 |\n| format_reward | 0.2 | E9 |\n| correct_meta_reward | 0.3 | E9 |\n| calibration_reward | 0.4 | E9 |\n| confidence_revision_reward | 0.6 | E9 |\n| overconfidence_penalty_reward | 1.0 | E9 |\n| length_penalty_reward | 1.0 | E9 |\n| effective_verification_reward | 0.9 | E9 |\n| overconfidence_verify_reward | 0.9 | E9 |\n| **same_route_repetition_penalty** | **0.5** | **NEW** |\n| **confidence_omission_floor** | **0.5** | **NEW** |\n\n---\n\n### E9bv2: Redirect Execution\n\n**Node**: TRAIN_B (GPU 0-3, dedicated training lane)\n\n**Intent**: Ensure that redirect rewards require structural evidence of a route switch in the solve body, not just a non-empty tail. The current reward fires whenever the model writes anything after announcing a redirect, even if that \"anything\" continues the original approach.\n\n**Hypothesis**: Replacing `bool(solve_tail.strip())` with `route_switch_evidence_reward` (+0.9 for structural method-keyword difference between pre-meta and post-meta, -0.3 for announced switch without evidence) will increase `diagnosis_with_recovery` rate from 0/4 (E10) to >50% on the AIME + MATH-hard slice.\n\n**Mechanism**: The new reward extracts method keywords (algebra, geometry, combinatorics, number theory, substitution, casework, induction, parity, modular, generating function, etc.) from (a) the pre-meta solve body and (b) the post-meta solve tail. If the two keyword sets overlap <50%, the redirect is classified as a genuine route switch. If they overlap >80% and the meta announced a switch, the penalty fires.\n\n**Verification**:\n- **Primary metric**: `diagnosis_with_recovery / total_diagnosis` ratio on AIME (30) + MATH-hard (top-50 by difficulty) slice. Target: >50%.\n- **Secondary metric**: Method keyword Jaccard distance between pre-meta prefix and post-meta tail. Target: mean distance >0.3 for redirect cases.\n- **Falsification condition**: If models stop announcing redirects entirely (redirect_count drops from E9b's current level by >80%), the penalty weight is too harsh and should be reduced to 0.15.\n\n**Reward composition**:\n\n| Reward function | Weight | Source |\n|---|---|---|\n| correctness_reward | 3.0 | E9b |\n| format_reward | 0.2 | E9b |\n| correct_meta_reward | 0.3 | E9b |\n| calibration_reward | 0.4 | E9b |\n| confidence_revision_reward | 0.6 | E9b |\n| overconfidence_penalty_reward | 1.0 | E9b |\n| length_penalty_reward | 1.0 | E9b |\n| effective_redirection_reward | 1.0 | E9b (modified: tail check replaced) |\n| **route_switch_evidence_reward** | **0.6** | **NEW** |\n| **confidence_omission_floor** | **0.5** | **NEW** |\n\n---\n\n### E10v2: Full Controller + Coverage Floor\n\n**Node**: E8 (GPU 0-3, dedicated training lane)\n\n**Intent**: Combine improved verify and redirect with mandatory meta emission. E10 failed because the model escaped calibration by omitting confidence. E10v2 adds a coverage floor that penalizes missing meta, forcing the model to emit confidence so that verify and redirect rewards can shape its behavior.\n\n**Hypothesis**: `confidence_omission_floor` (-0.5 for completions with no parseable meta block) will increase confidence coverage from 5.6% (E10) to >60%, while `same_route_repetition_penalty` and `route_switch_evidence_reward` improve execution quality. Overall accuracy should remain >= 38% (within 4.2 percentage points of base SFT 42.2%).\n\n**Mechanism**: Three new rewards are added on top of the E10 base:\n1. `confidence_omission_floor`: Returns -0.5 when no meta block with parseable confidence exists, 0.0 otherwise. This makes omission costly without prescribing what confidence should be.\n2. `same_route_repetition_penalty`: Same as E9v2. Penalizes decorative verify.\n3. `route_switch_evidence_reward`: Same as E9bv2. Requires structural evidence for redirect.\n\n**Verification**:\n- **Primary metric**: `confidence_coverage > 60%` AND `accuracy >= 38%`. Both must hold simultaneously.\n- **Secondary metric**: Failure mode distribution shift. `no_meta_signal` should drop from 53/58 wrong answers (E10) to <10/58.\n- **Falsification condition**: If accuracy drops below 30%, the combined reward pressure from 16 reward functions is too strong and non-correctness weights should be uniformly scaled by 0.5x.\n\n**Reward composition**:\n\n| Reward function | Weight | Source |\n|---|---|---|\n| correctness_reward | 3.0 | E10 |\n| format_reward | 0.2 | E10 |\n| correct_meta_reward | 0.3 | E10 |\n| calibration_reward | 0.4 | E10 |\n| confidence_revision_reward | 0.6 | E10 |\n| overconfidence_penalty_reward | 1.0 | E10 |\n| length_penalty_reward | 1.0 | E10 |\n| effective_verification_reward | 0.8 | E10 |\n| effective_redirection_reward | 1.0 | E10 (modified: tail check replaced) |\n| diagnosis_reward | 0.6 | E10 |\n| decomposition_reward | 0.6 | E10 |\n| anomaly_notice_reward | 0.4 | E10 |\n| repeated_intervention_reward | 0.5 | E10 |\n| overconfidence_verify_reward | 1.0 | E10 |\n| **same_route_repetition_penalty** | **0.5** | **NEW** |\n| **route_switch_evidence_reward** | **0.6** | **NEW** |\n| **confidence_omission_floor** | **0.5** | **NEW** |\n\n---\n\n## 4. New Reward Functions (Exact Specifications)\n\n### 4.1 `same_route_repetition_penalty`\n\n```python\ndef same_route_repetition_penalty(completions, ground_truth=None, **kwargs):\n    \"\"\"Penalize verification that restates the same derivation.\n    \n    Computes character trigram overlap between the pre-meta solve body\n    and the post-meta solve tail. If overlap > 0.7, returns -1.0.\n    If overlap 0.5-0.7, returns -0.3. Otherwise 0.0.\n    Only fires when verify intent is detected in meta.\n    \"\"\"\n```\n\n| Condition | Reward |\n|---|---|\n| No verify intent in meta | 0.0 |\n| Verify intent + trigram overlap > 0.7 | -1.0 |\n| Verify intent + trigram overlap 0.5-0.7 | -0.3 |\n| Verify intent + trigram overlap < 0.5 | 0.0 |\n\nWeight in E9v2: 0.5. Weight in E10v2: 0.5.\n\n### 4.2 `route_switch_evidence_reward`\n\n```python\ndef route_switch_evidence_reward(completions, ground_truth=None, **kwargs):\n    \"\"\"Reward structural method difference between pre-meta and post-meta.\n    \n    Extracts method keywords from pre-meta prefix and post-meta tail.\n    Rewards genuine route switches; penalizes announced-but-not-executed switches.\n    \"\"\"\n```\n\n| Condition | Reward |\n|---|---|\n| No redirect signal in meta | 0.0 |\n| Redirect signal + keyword Jaccard distance > 0.5 (genuine switch) + correct | +1.5 |\n| Redirect signal + keyword Jaccard distance > 0.5 (genuine switch) + wrong | +0.3 |\n| Redirect signal + keyword Jaccard distance < 0.2 (fake switch) | -0.5 |\n| Redirect signal + keyword Jaccard distance 0.2-0.5 (ambiguous) | 0.0 |\n\nWeight in E9bv2: 0.6. Weight in E10v2: 0.6.\n\n### 4.3 `confidence_omission_floor`\n\n```python\ndef confidence_omission_floor(completions, ground_truth=None, **kwargs):\n    \"\"\"Penalize completions that omit meta/confidence entirely.\n    \n    Returns -1.0 if no meta block with parseable confidence exists.\n    Returns 0.0 otherwise.\n    This prevents the model from escaping calibration pressure by omitting meta.\n    \"\"\"\n```\n\n| Condition | Reward |\n|---|---|\n| At least one meta block with parseable confidence | 0.0 |\n| No meta block OR no parseable confidence in any block | -1.0 |\n\nWeight in all v2 experiments: 0.5. Effective penalty for omission: -0.5.\n\n### 4.4 Modification to `effective_redirection_reward` (E9bv2, E10v2 only)\n\nLine 1051 changes from:\n```python\nhas_tail_recovery = bool(solve_tail.strip())\n```\nto:\n```python\nhas_tail_recovery = _has_route_switch_in_tail(solve_tail, text)\n```\n\nwhere `_has_route_switch_in_tail` checks for method-keyword divergence (same logic as `route_switch_evidence_reward` but returns bool). This is the **only modification** to an existing reward function. First pass: compute group accuracy\n   684\t    correct_flags = []\n   685\t    for i, c in enumerate(completions):\n   686\t        text = _get_text(c)\n   687\t        gt = ground_truth[i] if ground_truth is not None else \"\"\n   688\t        correct_flags.append(1.0 if _check_correctness(text, gt) else 0.0)\n   689\t    group_accuracy = sum(correct_flags) / max(len(correct_flags), 1)\n   690\t\n   691\t    # Second pass: compute calibration reward per completion\n   692\t    rewards = []\n   693\t    for i, c in enumerate(completions):\n   694\t        text = _get_text(c)\n   695\t        blocks = _parse_meta_blocks(text)\n   696\t\n   697\t        if not blocks or all(b[\"confidence\"] is None for b in blocks):\n   698\t            rewards.append(0.0)\n   699\t            continue\n   700\t\n   701\t        r = 0.0\n   702\t        n = 0\n   703\t        for block in blocks:\n   704\t            conf = block[\"confidence\"]\n   705\t            if conf is None:\n   706\t                continue\n   707\t            # average\n   727\t        rewards.append(max(r, -5.0))\n   728\t    return rewards\n   729\t\n   730\t\n   731\t# ─── R4: Uncertainty-Aware Meta ───\n   732\t\n   733\tdef uncertainty_meta_reward(completions, ground_truth=None, **kwargs):\n   734\t    \"\"\"Higher reward when meta blocks appear at uncertain moments.\n   735\t\n   736\t    (1 - confidence) × meta_quality → summation\n   737\t    Uncertain + good meta = high reward\n   738\t    Confident + any meta = low reward (unnecessary reflection)\n   739\t    \"\"\"\n   740\t    rewards = []\n   741\t    for i, c in enumerate(completions):\n   742\t        text = _get_text(c)\n   743\t        blocks = _parse_meta_blocks(text)\n   744\t\n   745\t        if not blocks:\n   746\t            rewards.append(0.0)\n   747\t            continue\n   748\t\n   749\t        r = 0.0\n   750\t        for block in blocks[:4]:\n   751\t            conf = block[\"confidence\"]\n   752\t            if conf is None:\n   753\t                conf = 0.5  # unknown confidence treated as moderate\n   754\t\n   755\t            uncertainty = 1.0 - conf  # high when unsure\n   756\t\n   757\t            # Quality component\n   758\t            quality = 0.0\n   759\t            if block[\"length\"] >= 10:\n   760\t                quality += 0.5\n   761\t            if re.search(r'[?？]', block[\"text\"]):\n   762\t                quality += 0.5\n   763\t            quality = min(quality, 1.0)\n   764\t\n   765\t            r += uncertainty * quality  # The intended object\n   777\t    is each meta intervention:\n   778\t      - early blocks should avoid unjustified overconfidence\n   779\t      - anomaly/diagnosis blocks should revise confidence downward\n   780\t      - final blocks should calibrate confidence to outcome\n   781\t    \"\"\"\n   782\t    rewards = []\n   783\t    for i, c in enumerate(completions):\n   784\t        text = _get_text(c)\n   785\t        gt = ground_truth[i] if ground_truth is not None else \"\"\n   786\t        is_correct = _check_correctness(text, gt)\n   787\t        rewards.append(_score_stepwise_blocks(text, is_correct=is_correct))\n   788\t    return rewards\n   789\t\n   790\t\n   791\t# ─── R6: Probe Calibration Reward ───\n   792\tdef stepwise_probe_reward(completions, ground_truth=None, **kwargs):\n   793\t    \"\"\"Probe-based stepwise reward with per-meta-block credit assignment.\n   794\t\n   795\t    For each meta block, score stated confidence against probe-estimated local\n   796\t    correctness probability from the prefix ending at that block. probe_calibration_reward(completions, ground_truth=None,\n   833\t                              model=None, tokenizer=None, **kwargs):\n   834\t    \"\"\"Calibration reward using a hidden-state probe 838\t\n   839\t        R = mean_k [ -(conf_k - p_hat_k)^2 ]\n   840\t\n   841\t    This is the verifiable bridge between verbal confidence and internal belief.\n   842\t    \"\"\"\n   843\t sum(rewards) → group_normalize  (collapses distinct reward combos)\n   222\t    GDPO: group_normalize(each_reward) → sum → batch_normalize  (preserves signal)\n   223\t\n   224\t    Reference: arXiv:2601.05242 (NVIDIA NVlabs)\n   225\t    \"\"\"\n   226\t    import trl.trainer.grpo_trainer as grpo_module\n   227\t\n   228\t    original_method = GRPOTrainer._generate_and_score_completions\n if we have multiple reward functions\n   235\t        if not hasattr(self, '_gdpo_enabled') or not self._gdpo_enabled:\n   236\t            return result\n   237\t\n   238\t        # Re-compute advantages with GDPO\n   239\t        # Access rewards_per_func from the stored attribute\n   240\t        if hasattr(self, '_last_rewards_per_func') and self._last_rewards_per_func is not None:\n   241\t            rewards_per_func = self._last_rewards_per_func\n   242\t            device = rewards_per_func.device\n   243\t            num_gen = self.num_generations\n   244\t\n   245\t            all_adv = []\n   246\t            for i in range(rewards_per_func.shape[1]):\n   247\t                r_i = torch.nan_to_num(rewards_per_func[:, i])\n   248\t                mean_i = r_i.view(-1, num_gen).mean(dim=1)\n   249\t                std_i = r_i.view(-1, num_gen).std(dim=1)\n   250\t                mean_i = mean_i.repeat_interleave(num_gen, dim=0)\n   251\t                std_i = std_i.repeat_interleave(num_gen, dim=0)\n   252\t                adv_i = (r_i - mean_i) / (std_i + 1e-4)\n   253\t                all_adv.append(adv_i)\n   254\t\n   255\t            combined = torch.stack(all_adv, dim=1)\n   256\t            weights = self.reward_weights.to(device).unsqueeze(0)\n   257\t            pre_bn = (combined * weights).nansum(dim=1)\n   258\t            advantages = (pre_bn - pre_bn.mean()) / (pre_bn.std() + 1e-4)\n   259\t\n   260\t            # _last_rewards_per_func is LOCAL (per-process) from _calculate_rewards,\n","exit_code":0,"status":"completed"}}

results/experiment_plan_v5.md\\\"\",\"aggregated_output\":\"# Meta-CoT Experiment Plan v5: Fixing Meta Execution\\n\\n**Date**: 2026-04-04\\n**Author**: Seungpil Lee\\n**Project**: metacognition-math (Qwen3-8B)\\n**Predecessor**: experiment_plan_v4.md (accuracy-focused autoresearch loop)\\n\\n---\\n\\n## 1. Current State Summary\\n\\n### What works\\n\\n1. **Parseable meta**: The SFT-trained model emits well-formed `<|meta|>...<|/meta|>` blocks containing confidence, diagnosis, and strategy statements. Coverage reaches 88.9% on `all_sft`.\\n2. **Calibration (ECE reduction)**: E8 achieves ECE 0.322 with only 3.6% wrong-high-confidence, the best overconfidence suppression among all conditions.\\n3. **Overconfidence suppression (E8)**: `overconfidence_penalty_reward` + `confidence_revision_reward` successfully pushed wrong-high-conf from 80.7% (verify_sft) down to 3.6% (E8).\\n4. **Accuracy near parity (E9)**: E9 reaches 41.1% overall (base SFT: 42.2%), the closest Meta-CoT model to parity, driven by GSM8K 90.0%.\\n\\n### What does not work\\n\\n1. **Verify execution**: Verification is same-route repetition, not independent falsification. 15/53 wrong answers in E9 are overconfident-verify-failed: the model says \\\"verify\\\" then re-derives the same wrong answer (e.g., AIME 540 re-uses identical extremal intuition; GSM8K restart miscounts time identically).\\n2. **Redirect execution**: Diagnosis appears but the solve body continues the original route. 0/4 diagnosis cases in E10 led to actual recovery. `effective_redirection_reward` checks `bool(solve_tail.strip())` for recovery, so any non-empty tail passes regardless of whether it contains a route switch.\\n3. **Repeated intervention**: Hard problems get exactly one meta block. No ongoing controller loop is observed. The model treats meta as a one-shot annotation rather than an iterative self-monitor.\\n4. **Full controller (E10)**: Only 5.6% confidence coverage. 53 out of 58 wrong answers have no meta signal at all. The model learned to omit confidence to avoid calibration penalties.\\n\\n### Quantitative reference (n=90 pilot, 30 per benchmark)\\n\\n| Model | Acc | AIME | GSM8K | MATH500 | conf_cov | ECE | wrong_high_conf |\\n|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|\\n| base_sft | 42.2 | 13.3 | 80.0 | 33.3 | 0.0 | n/a | n/a |\\n| all_sft | 33.3 | 6.7 | 63.3 | 30.0 | 88.9 | 0.398 | 51.7 |\\n| E8 | 38.9 | 10.0 | 80.0 | 26.7 | 23.3 | 0.322 | 3.6 |\\n| E9 | 41.1 | 6.7 | 90.0 | 26.7 | 91.1 | 0.301 | 50.9 |\\n| E9b | 40.0 | 6.7 | 83.3 | 30.0 | 0.0 | n/a | n/a |\\n| E10 | 35.6 | 6.7 | 66.7 | 33.3 | 5.6 | 0.340 | 0.0 |\\n\\n---\\n\\n## 2. Root Cause Analysis\\n\\nThree code-level root causes explain why meta detection succeeds but meta execution fails.\\n\\n### Root Cause 1: `effective_verification_reward` rewards same-route repetition\\n\\n**Location**: `rewards.py` line 1016-1035, specifically `_has_effective_verification_signal` (line 119-125).\\n\\nThe function checks for word patterns (\\\"substitute\\\", \\\"plug back\\\", \\\"recalculat\\\") in the solve tail after the last meta block. The problem is that restating the same derivation with verification keywords counts as effective verification. There is no check for **structural independence** -- whether the verification method differs from the original solve route.\\n\\n**Consequence**: The model learns to append \\\"let me substitute back...\\\" followed by the same calculation. This gets rewarded at +0.8 for correct answers, reinforcing decorative verification.\\n\\n### Root Cause 2: `effective_redirection_reward` accepts any non-empty tail as recovery\\n\\n**Location**: `rewards.py` line 1038-1063, specifically line 1051: `has_tail_recovery = bool(solve_tail.strip())`.\\n\\nThe maximum reward (+1.0 for correct, +0.2 for wrong) requires `has_conflict and has_switch and has_drop and has_tail_recovery`. But `has_tail_recovery` is satisfied by any non-empty text after the last meta block -- including the original solve continuation that ignores the announced strategy switch.\\n\\n**Consequence**: The model announces \\\"switch to parity-based analysis\\\" in meta, then continues the original algebraic approach. Because the tail is non-empty, the redirection reward fires as if recovery occurred.\\n\\n### Root Cause 3: `calibration_reward` returns 0.0 for no meta, making omission cost-free\\n\\n**Location**: `rewards.py` line 656-710, specifically lines 679-680:\\n\\n```python\\nif not blocks or all(b[\\\"confidence\\\"] is None for b in blocks):\\n    rewards.append(0.0)\\n```\\n\\nWhen the model emits no meta blocks or omits confidence, it receives 0.0 from calibration. Meanwhile, emitting confidence on wrong answers risks negative reward from both the Brier component and the log scoring rule. Rational reward optimization therefore favors omitting confidence entirely.\\n\\n**Consequence**: E5 (conf_cov=1.1%), E9b (conf_cov=0.0%), and E10 (conf_cov=5.6%) all escaped calibration pressure by reducing meta emission. This makes calibration metrics uninterpretable and defeats the purpose of Meta-CoT.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## 3. Proposed Experiments\\n\\nAll three experiments start from the same SFT checkpoint: `qwen3_metacot_control_v5_all_sft`. This ensures the only variable is the reward composition.\\n\\n### E9v2: Verify Quality\\n\\n**Node**: EVAL (GPU 0-3, same as current eval lane)\\n\\n**Intent**: Teach the model that verification must use an independent method, not repeat the same calculation. The current verify reward conflates \\\"mentions verification keywords\\\" with \\\"actually performs a structurally different check.\\\"\\n\\n**Hypothesis**: Adding `same_route_repetition_penalty` (-0.5 when the solve tail after a verify announcement shares >70% n-gram overlap with the pre-meta solve body) will reduce `overconfident_verify_failed` rate from 15/53 (28.3%, E9) to <5/53 (9.4%) without reducing overall accuracy by more than 2 percentage points.\\n\\n**Mechanism**: The new penalty computes character trigram overlap between the pre-meta solve prefix and the post-meta solve tail. If overlap exceeds 70%, the verification is classified as same-route repetition. The existing `effective_verification_reward` remains unchanged -- the penalty is additive, creating a gradient between \\\"verify with a new method (+0.8)\\\" and \\\"verify by restating (-0.5).\\\"\\n\\n**Verification**:\\n- **Primary metric**: `overconfident_verify_failed` count on 1,030-problem eval. Target: <10% of wrong answers (currently 28.3%).\\n- **Secondary metric**: `independent_method_rate` = fraction of verify completions where trigram overlap <70%. Target: >50%.\\n- **Falsification condition**: If `wrong_high_conf` stays >40% despite the penalty, the trigram heuristic is too weak to detect repetition and a stronger structural check (e.g., operation-type extraction) is needed.\\n\\n**Reward composition**:\\n\\n| Reward function | Weight | Source |\\n|---|---|---|\\n| correctness_reward | 3.0 | E9 |\\n| format_reward | 0.2 | E9 |\\n| correct_meta_reward | 0.3 | E9 |\\n| calibration_reward | 0.4 | E9 |\\n| confidence_revision_reward | 0.6 | E9 |\\n| overconfidence_penalty_reward | 1.0 | E9 |\\n| length_penalty_reward | 1.0 | E9 |\\n| effective_verification_reward | 0.9 | E9 |\\n| overconfidence_verify_reward | 0.9 | E9 |\\n| **same_route_repetition_penalty** | **0.5** | **NEW** |\\n| **confidence_omission_floor** | **0.5** | **NEW** |\\n\\n---\\n\\n### E9bv2: Redirect Execution\\n\\n**Node**: TRAIN_B (GPU 0-3, dedicated training lane)\\n\\n**Intent**: Ensure that redirect rewards require structural evidence of a route switch in the solve body, not just a non-empty tail. The current reward fires whenever the model writes anything after announcing a redirect, even if that \\\"anything\\\" continues the original approach.\\n\\n**Hypothesis**: Replacing `bool(solve_tail.strip())` with `route_switch_evidence_reward` (+0.9 for structural method-keyword difference between pre-meta and post-meta, -0.3 for announced switch without evidence) will increase `diagnosis_with_recovery` rate from 0/4 (E10) to >50% on the AIME + MATH-hard slice.\\n\\n**Mechanism**: The new reward extracts method keywords (algebra, geometry, combinatorics, number theory, substitution, casework, induction, parity, modular, generating function, etc.) from (a) the pre-meta solve body and (b) the post-meta solve tail. If the two keyword sets overlap <50%, the redirect is classified as a genuine route switch. If they overlap >80% and the meta announced a switch, the penalty fires.\\n\\n**Verification**:\\n- **Primary metric**: `diagnosis_with_recovery / total_diagnosis` ratio on AIME (30) + MATH-hard (top-50 by difficulty) slice. Target: >50%.\\n- **Secondary metric**: Method keyword Jaccard distance between pre-meta prefix and post-meta tail. Target: mean distance >0.3 for redirect cases.\\n- **Falsification condition**: If models stop announcing redirects entirely (redirect_count drops from E9b's current level by >80%), the penalty weight is too harsh and should be reduced to 0.15.\\n\\n**Reward composition**:\\n\\n| Reward function | Weight | Source |\\n|---|---|---|\\n| correctness_reward | 3.0 | E9b |\\n| format_reward | 0.2 | E9b |\\n| correct_meta_reward | 0.3 | E9b |\\n| calibration_reward | 0.4 | E9b |\\n| confidence_revision_reward | 0.6 | E9b |\\n| overconfidence_penalty_reward | 1.0 | E9b |\\n| length_penalty_reward | 1.0 | E9b |\\n| effective_redirection_reward | 1.0 | E9b (modified: tail check replaced) |\\n| **route_switch_evidence_reward** | **0.6** | **NEW** |\\n| **confidence_omission_floor** | **0.5** | **NEW** |\\n\\n---\\n\\n### E10v2: Full Controller + Coverage Floor\\n\\n**Node**: E8 (GPU 0-3, dedicated training lane)\\n\\n**Intent**: Combine improved verify and redirect with mandatory meta emission. E10 failed because the model escaped calibration by omitting confidence. E10v2 adds a coverage floor that penalizes missing meta, forcing the model to emit confidence so that verify and redirect rewards can shape its behavior.\\n\\n**Hypothesis**: `confidence_omission_floor` (-0.5 for completions with no parseable meta block) will increase confidence coverage from 5.6% (E10) to >60%, while `same_route_repetition_penalty` and `route_switch_evidence_reward` improve execution quality. Overall accuracy should remain >= 38% (within 4.2 percentage points of base SFT 42.2%).\\n\\n**Mechanism**: Three new rewards are added on top of the E10 base:\\n1. `confidence_omission_floor`: Returns -0.5 when no meta block with parseable confidence exists, 0.0 otherwise. This makes omission costly without prescribing what confidence should be.\\n2. `same_route_repetition_penalty`: Same as E9v2. Penalizes decorative verify.\\n3. `route_switch_evidence_reward`: Same as E9bv2. Requires structural evidence for redirect.\\n\\n**Verification**:\\n- **Primary metric**: `confidence_coverage > 60%` AND `accuracy >= 38%`. Both must hold simultaneously.\\n- **Secondary metric**: Failure mode distribution shift. `no_meta_signal` should drop from 53/58 wrong answers (E10) to <10/58.\\n- **Falsification condition**: If accuracy drops below 30%, the combined reward pressure from 16 reward functions is too strong and non-correctness weights should be uniformly scaled by 0.5x.\\n\\n**Reward composition**:\\n\\n| Reward function | Weight | Source |\\n|---|---|---|\\n| correctness_reward | 3.0 | E10 |\\n| format_reward | 0.2 | E10 |\\n| correct_meta_reward | 0.3 | E10 |\\n| calibration_reward | 0.4 | E10 |\\n| confidence_revision_reward | 0.6 | E10 |\\n| overconfidence_penalty_reward | 1.0 | E10 |\\n| length_penalty_reward | 1.0 | E10 |\\n| effective_verification_reward | 0.8 | E10 |\\n| effective_redirection_reward | 1.0 | E10 (modified: tail check replaced) |\\n| diagnosis_reward | 0.6 | E10 |\\n| decomposition_reward | 0.6 | E10 |\\n| anomaly_notice_reward | 0.4 | E10 |\\n| repeated_intervention_reward | 0.5 | E10 |\\n| overconfidence_verify_reward | 1.0 | E10 |\\n| **same_route_repetition_penalty** | **0.5** | **NEW** |\\n| **route_switch_evidence_reward** | **0.6** | **NEW** |\\n| **confidence_omission_floor** | **0.5** | **NEW** |\\n\\n---\\n\\n## 4. Current State Summary\\n\\n### What works\\n\\n1. **Parseable meta**: The SFT-trained model emits well-formed `<|meta|>...<|/meta|>` blocks containing confidence, diagnosis, and strategy statements. Coverage reaches 88.9% on `all_sft`.\\n2. **Calibration (ECE reduction)**: E8 achieves ECE 0.322 with only 3.6% wrong-high-confidence, the best overconfidence suppression among all conditions.\\n3. **Overconfidence suppression (E8)**: `overconfidence_penalty_reward` + `confidence_revision_reward` successfully pushed wrong-high-conf from 80.7% (verify_sft) down to 3.6% (E8).\\n4. **Accuracy near parity (E9)**: E9 reaches 41.1% overall (base SFT: 42.2%), the closest Meta-CoT model to parity, driven by GSM8K 90.0%.\\n\\n### What does not work\\n\\n1. **Verify execution**: Verification is same-route repetition, not independent falsification. 15/53 wrong answers in E9 are overconfident-verify-failed: the model says \\\"verify\\\" then re-derives the same wrong answer (e.g., AIME 540 re-uses identical extremal intuition; GSM8K restart miscounts time identically).\\n2. **Redirect execution**: Diagnosis appears but the solve body continues the original route. 0/4 diagnosis cases in E10 led to actual recovery. `effective_redirection_reward` checks `bool(solve_tail.strip())` for recovery, so any non-empty tail passes regardless of whether it contains a route switch.\\n3. **Repeated intervention**: Hard problems get exactly one meta block. No ongoing controller loop is observed. The model treats meta as a one-shot annotation rather than an iterative self-monitor.\\n4. **Full controller (E10)**: Only 5.6% confidence coverage. 53 out of 58 wrong answers have no meta signal at all. The model learned to omit confidence to avoid calibration penalties.\\n\\n### Quantitative reference (n=90 pilot, 30 per benchmark)\\n\\n| Model | Acc | AIME | GSM8K | MATH500 | conf_cov | ECE | wrong_high_conf |\\n|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|\\n| base_sft | 42.2 | 13.3 | 80.0 | 33.3 | 0.0 | n/a | n/a |\\n| all_sft | 33.3 | 6.7 | 63.3 | 30.0 | 88.9 | 0.398 | 51.7 |\\n| E8 | 38.9 | 10.0 | 80.0 | 26.7 | 23.3 | 0.322 | 3.6 |\\n| E9 | 41.1 | 6.7 | 90.0 | 26.7 | 91.1 | 0.301 | 50.9 |\\n| E9b | 40.0 | 6.7 | 83.3 | 30.0 | 0.0 | n/a | n/a |\\n| E10 | 35.6 | 6.7 | 66.7 | 33.3 | 5.6 | 0.340 | 0.0 |\\n\\n---\\n\\n## 2. Root Cause Analysis\\n\\nThree code-level root causes explain why meta detection succeeds but meta execution fails.\\n\\n### Root Cause 1: `effective_verification_reward` rewards same-route repetition\\n\\n**Location**: `rewards.py` line 1016-1035, specifically `_has_effective_verification_signal` (line 119-125).\\n\\nThe function checks for word patterns (\\\"substitute\\\", \\\"plug back\\\", \\\"recalculat\\\") in the solve tail after the last meta block. The problem is that restating the same derivation with verification keywords counts as effective verification. There is no check for **structural independence** -- whether the verification method differs from the original solve route.\\n\\n**Consequence**: The model learns to append \\\"let me substitute back...\\\" followed by the same calculation. This gets rewarded at +0.8 for correct answers, reinforcing decorative verification.\\n\\n### Root Cause 2: `effective_redirection_reward` accepts any non-empty tail as recovery\\n\\n**Location**: `rewards.py` line 1038-1063, specifically line 1051: `has_tail_recovery = bool(solve_tail.strip())`.\\n\\nThe maximum reward (+1.0 for correct, +0.2 for wrong) requires `has_conflict and has_switch and has_drop and has_tail_recovery`. But `has_tail_recovery` is satisfied by any non-empty text after the last meta block -- including the original solve continuation that ignores the announced strategy switch.\\n\\n**Consequence**: The model announces \\\"switch to parity-based analysis\\\" in meta, then continues the original algebraic approach. Because the tail is non-empty, the redirection reward fires as if recovery occurred.\\n\\n### Root Cause 3: `calibration_reward` returns 0.0 for no meta, making omission cost-free\\n\\n**Location**: `rewards.py` line 656-710, specifically lines 679-680:\\n\\n```python\\nif not blocks or all(b[\\\"confidence\\\"] is None for b in blocks):\\n    rewards.append(0.0)\\n```\\n\\nWhen the model emits no meta blocks or omits confidence, it receives 0.0 from calibration. Meanwhile, emitting confidence on wrong answers risks negative reward from both the Brier component and the log scoring rule. Rational reward optimization therefore favors omitting confidence entirely.\\n\\n**Consequence**: E5 (conf_cov=1.1%), E9b (conf_cov=0.0%), and E10 (conf_cov=5.6%) all escaped calibration pressure by reducing meta emission. This makes calibration metrics uninterpretable and defeats the purpose of Meta-CoT.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## 3. Proposed Experiments\\n\\nAll three experiments start from the same SFT checkpoint: `qwen3_metacot_control_v5_all_sft`. This ensures the only variable is the reward composition.\\n\\n### E9v2: Verify Quality\\n\\n**Node**: EVAL (GPU 0-3, same as current eval lane)\\n\\n**Intent**: Teach the model that verification must use an independent method, not repeat the same calculation. The current verify reward conflates \\\"mentions verification keywords\\\" with \\\"actually performs a structurally different check.\\\"\\n\\n**Hypothesis**: Adding `same_route_repetition_penalty` (-0.5 when the solve tail after a verify announcement shares >70% n-gram overlap with the pre-meta solve body) will reduce `overconfident_verify_failed` rate from 15/53 (28.3%, E9) to <5/53 (9.4%) without reducing overall accuracy by more than 2 percentage points.\\n\\n**Mechanism**: The new penalty computes character trigram overlap between the pre-meta solve prefix and the post-meta solve tail. If overlap exceeds 70%, the verification is classified as same-route repetition. The existing `effective_verification_reward` remains unchanged -- the penalty is additive, creating a gradient between \\\"verify with a new method (+0.8)\\\" and \\\"verify by restating (-0.5).\\\"\\n\\n**Verification**:\\n- **Primary metric**: `overconfident_verify_failed` count on 1,030-problem eval. Target: <10% of wrong answers (currently 28.3%).\\n- **Secondary metric**: `independent_method_rate` = fraction of verify completions where trigram overlap <70%. Target: >50%.\\n- **Falsification condition**: If `wrong_high_conf` stays >40% despite the penalty, the trigram heuristic is too weak to detect repetition and a stronger structural check (e.g., operation-type extraction) is needed.\\n\\n**Reward composition**:\\n\\n| Reward function | Weight | Source |\\n|---|---|---|\\n| correctness_reward | 3.0 | E9 |\\n| format_reward | 0.2 | E9 |\\n| correct_meta_reward | 0.3 | E9 |\\n| calibration_reward | 0.4 | E9 |\\n| confidence_revision_reward | 0.6 | E9 |\\n| overconfidence_penalty_reward | 1.0 | E9 |\\n| length_penalty_reward | 1.0 | E9 |\\n| effective_verification_reward | 0.9 | E9 |\\n| overconfidence_verify_reward | 0.9 | E9 |\\n| **same_route_repetition_penalty** | **0.5** | **NEW** |\\n| **confidence_omission_floor** | **0.5** | **NEW** |\\n\\n---\\n\\n### E9bv2: Redirect Execution\\n\\n**Node**: TRAIN_B (GPU 0-3, dedicated training lane)\\n\\n**Intent**: Ensure that redirect rewards require structural evidence of a route switch in the solve body, not just a non-empty tail. |\\nresults/codex_reviews/plan_review_1_log.txt:9:{\\\"type\\\":\\\"item.completed\\\",\\\"item\\\":{\\\"id\\\":\\\"item_3\\\",\\\"type\\\":\\\"command_execution\\\",\\\"command\\\":\\\"/bin/bash -lc \\\\\\\"sed -n '1,260p' results/experiment_plan_v5.md\\\\\\\"\\\",\\\"aggregated_output\\\":\\\"# Meta-CoT Experiment Plan v5: Fixing Meta Execution\\\\n\\\\n**Date**: 2026-04-04\\\\n**Author**: Seungpil Lee\\\\n**Project**: metacognition-math (Qwen3-8B)\\\\n**Predecessor**: experiment_plan_v4.md (accuracy-focused autoresearch loop)\\\\n\\\\n---\\\\n\\\\n## 1. Current State Summary\\\\n\\\\n### What works\\\\n\\\\n1. **Parseable meta**: The SFT-trained model emits well-formed `<|meta|>...<|/meta|>` blocks containing confidence, diagnosis, and strategy statements. Coverage reaches 88.9% on `all_sft`.\\\\n2. **Calibration (ECE reduction)**: E8 achieves ECE 0.322 with only 3.6% wrong-high-confidence, the best overconfidence suppression among all conditions.\\\\n3. **Overconfidence suppression (E8)**: `overconfidence_penalty_reward` + `confidence_revision_reward` successfully pushed wrong-high-conf from 80.7% (verify_sft) down to 3.6% (E8).\\\\n4. **Accuracy near parity (E9)**: E9 reaches 41.1% overall (base SFT: 42.2%), the closest Meta-CoT model to parity, driven by GSM8K 90.0%.\\\\n\\\\n### What does not work\\\\n\\\\n1. **Verify execution**: Verification is same-route repetition, not independent falsification. 15/53 wrong answers in E9 are overconfident-verify-failed: the model says \\\\\\\"verify\\\\\\\" then re-derives the same wrong answer (e.g., AIME 540 re-uses identical extremal intuition; GSM8K restart miscounts time identically).\\\\n2. **Redirect execution**: Diagnosis appears but the solve body continues the original route. 0/4 diagnosis cases in E10 led to actual recovery. `effective_redirection_reward` checks `bool(solve_tail.strip())` for recovery, so any non-empty tail passes regardless of whether it contains a route switch.\\\\n3. **Repeated intervention**: Hard problems get exactly one meta block. No ongoing controller loop is observed. The model treats meta as a one-shot annotation rather than an iterative self-monitor.\\\\n4. **Full controller (E10)**: Only 5.6% confidence coverage. 53 out of 58 wrong answers have no meta signal at all. The model learned to omit confidence to avoid calibration penalties.\\\\n\\\\n### Quantitative reference (n=90 pilot, 30 per benchmark)\\\\n\\\\n| Model | Acc | AIME | GSM8K | MATH500 | conf_cov | ECE | wrong_high_conf |\\\\n|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|\\\\n| base_sft | 42.2 | 13.3 | 80.0 | 33.3 | 0.0 | n/a | n/a |\\\\n| all_sft | 33.3 | 6.7 | 63.3 | 30.0 | 88.9 | 0.398 | 51.7 |\\\\n| E8 | 38.9 | 10.0 | 80.0 | 26.7 | 23.3 | 0.322 | 3.6 |\\\\n| E9 | 41.1 | 6.7 | 90.0 | 26.7 | 91.1 | 0.301 | 50.9 |\\\\n| E9b | 40.0 | 6.7 | 83.3 | 30.0 | 0.0 | n/a | n/a |\\\\n| E10 | 35.6 | 6.7 | 66.7 | 33.3 | 5.6 | 0.340 | 0.0 |\\\\n\\\\n---\\\\n\\\\n## 2. Root Cause Analysis\\\\n\\\\nThree code-level root causes explain why meta detection succeeds but meta execution fails.\\\\n\\\\n### Root Cause 1: `effective_verification_reward` rewards same-route repetition\\\\n\\\\n**Location**: `rewards.py` line 1016-1035, specifically `_has_effective_verification_signal` (line 119-125).\\\\n\\\\nThe function checks for word patterns (\\\\\\\"substitute\\\\\\\", \\\\\\\"plug back\\\\\\\", \\\\\\\"recalculat\\\\\\\") in the solve tail after the last meta block. The problem is that restating the same derivation with verification keywords counts as effective verification. There is no check for **structural independence** -- whether the verification method differs from the original solve route.\\\\n\\\\n**Consequence**: The model learns to append \\\\\\\"let me substitute back...\\\\\\\" followed by the same calculation. This gets rewarded at +0.8 for correct answers, reinforcing decorative verification.\\\\n\\\\n### Root Cause 2: `effective_redirection_reward` accepts any non-empty tail as recovery\\\\n\\\\n**Location**: `rewards.py` line 1038-1063, specifically line 1051: `has_tail_recovery = bool(solve_tail.strip())`.\\\\n\\\\nThe maximum reward (+1.0 for correct, +0.2 for wrong) requires `has_conflict and has_switch and has_drop and has_tail_recovery`. But `has_tail_recovery` is satisfied by any non-empty text after the last meta block -- including the original solve continuation that ignores the announced strategy switch.\\\\n\\\\n**Consequence**: The model announces \\\\\\\"switch to parity-based analysis\\\\\\\" in meta, then continues the original algebraic approach. Because the tail is non-empty, the redirection reward fires as if recovery occurred.\\\\n\\\\n### Root Cause 3: `calibration_reward` returns 0.0 for no meta, making omission cost-free\\\\n\\\\n**Location**: `rewards.py` line 656-710, specifically lines 679-680:\\\\n\\\\n```python\\\\nif not blocks or all(b[\\\\\\\"confidence\\\\\\\"] is None for b in blocks):\\\\n    rewards.append(0.0)\\\\n```\\\\n\\\\nWhen the model emits no meta blocks or omits confidence, it receives 0.0 from calibration. Meanwhile, emitting confidence on wrong answers risks negative reward from both the Brier component and the log scoring rule. Rational reward optimization therefore favors omitting confidence entirely.\\\\n\\\\n**Consequence**: E5 (conf_cov=1.1%), E9b (conf_cov=0.0%), and E10 (conf_cov=5.6%) all escaped calibration pressure by reducing meta emission. This makes calibration metrics uninterpretable and defeats the purpose of Meta-CoT.\\\\n\\\\n---\\\\n\\\\n## 3. Proposed Experiments\\\\n\\\\nAll three experiments start from the same SFT checkpoint: `qwen3_metacot_control_v5_all_sft`. This ensures the only variable is the reward composition.\\\\n\\\\n### E9v2: Verify Quality\\\\n\\\\n**Node**: EVAL (GPU 0-3, same as current eval lane)\\\\n\\\\n**Intent**: Teach the model that verification must use an independent method, not repeat the same calculation. The current verify reward conflates \\\\\\\"mentions verification keywords\\\\\\\" with \\\\\\\"actually performs a structurally different check.\\\\\\\"\\\\n\\\\n**Hypothesis**: Adding `same_route_repetition_penalty` (-0.5 when the solve tail after a verify announcement shares >70% n-gram overlap with the pre-meta solve body) will reduce `overconfident_verify_failed` rate from 15/53 (28.3%, E9) to <5/53 (9.4%) without reducing overall accuracy by more than 2 percentage points.\\\\n\\\\n**Mechanism**: The new penalty computes character trigram overlap between the pre-meta solve prefix and the post-meta solve tail. If overlap exceeds 70%, the verification is classified as same-route repetition. The existing `effective_verification_reward` remains unchanged -- the penalty is additive, creating a gradient between \\\\\\\"verify with a new method (+0.8)\\\\\\\" and \\\\\\\"verify by restating (-0.5).\\\\\\\"\\\\n\\\\n**Verification**:\\\\n- **Primary metric**: `overconfident_verify_failed` count on 1,030-problem eval. Target: <10% of wrong answers (currently 28.3%).\\\\n- **Secondary metric**: `independent_method_rate` = fraction of verify completions where trigram overlap <70%. Target: >50%.\\\\n- **Falsification condition**: If `wrong_high_conf` stays >40% despite the penalty, the trigram heuristic is too weak to detect repetition and a stronger structural check (e.g., operation-type extraction) is needed.\\\\n\\\\n**Reward composition**:\\\\n\\\\n| Reward function | Weight | Source |\\\\n|---|---|---|\\\\n| correctness_reward | 3.0 | E9 |\\\\n| format_reward | 0.2 | E9 |\\\\n| correct_meta_reward | 0.3 | E9 |\\\\n| calibration_reward | 0.4 | E9 |\\\\n| confidence_revision_reward | 0.6 | E9 |\\\\n| overconfidence_penalty_reward | 1.0 | E9 |\\\\n| length_penalty_reward | 1.0 | E9 |\\\\n| effective_verification_reward | 0.9 | E9 |\\\\n| overconfidence_verify_reward | 0.9 | E9 |\\\\n| **same_route_repetition_penalty** | **0.5** | **NEW** |\\\\n| **confidence_omission_floor** | **0.5** | **NEW** |\\\\n\\\\n---\\\\n\\\\n### E9bv2: Redirect Execution\\\\n\\\\n**Node**: TRAIN_B (GPU 0-3, dedicated training lane)\\\\n\\\\n**Intent**: Ensure that redirect rewards require structural evidence of a route switch in the solve body, not just a non-empty tail. The current reward fires whenever the model writes anything after announcing a redirect, even if that \\\\\\\"anything\\\\\\\" continues the original approach.\\\\n\\\\n**Hypothesis**: Replacing `bool(solve_tail.strip())` with `route_switch_evidence_reward` (+0.9 for structural method-keyword difference between pre-meta and post-meta, -0.3 for announced switch without evidence) will increase `diagnosis_with_recovery` rate from 0/4 (E10) to >50% on the AIME + MATH-hard slice.\\\\n\\\\n**Mechanism**: The new reward extracts method keywords (algebra, geometry, combinatorics, number theory, substitution, casework, induction, parity, modular, generating function, etc.) from (a) the pre-meta solve body and (b) the post-meta solve tail. If the two keyword sets overlap <50%, the redirect is classified as a genuine route switch. If they overlap >80% and the meta announced a switch, the penalty fires.\\\\n\\\\n**Verification**:\\\\n- **Primary metric**: `diagnosis_with_recovery / total_diagnosis` ratio on AIME (30) + MATH-hard (top-50 by difficulty) slice. Target: >50%.\\\\n- **Secondary metric**: Method keyword Jaccard distance between pre-meta prefix and post-meta tail. Target: mean distance >0.3 for redirect cases.\\\\n- **Falsification condition**: If models stop announcing redirects entirely (redirect_count drops from E9b's current level by >80%), the penalty weight is too harsh and should be reduced to 0.15.\\\\n\\\\n**Reward composition**:\\\\n\\\\n| Reward function | Weight | Source |\\\\n|---|---|---|\\\\n| correctness_reward | 3.0 | E9b |\\\\n| format_reward | 0.2 | E9b |\\\\n| correct_meta_reward | 0.3 | E9b |\\\\n| calibration_reward | 0.4 | E9b |\\\\n| confidence_revision_reward | 0.6 | E9b |\\\\n| overconfidence_penalty_reward | 1.0 | E9b |\\\\n| length_penalty_reward | 1.0 | E9b |\\\\n| effective_redirection_reward | 1.0 | E9b (modified: tail check replaced) |\\\\n| **route_switch_evidence_reward** | **0.6** | **NEW** |\\\\n| **confidence_omission_floor** | **0.5** | **NEW** |\\\\n\\\\n---\\\\n\\\\n### E10v2: Full Controller + Coverage Floor\\\\n\\\\n**Node**: E8 (GPU 0-3, dedicated training lane)\\\\n\\\\n**Intent**: Combine improved verify and redirect with mandatory meta emission. E10 failed because the model escaped calibration by omitting confidence. E10v2 adds a coverage floor that penalizes missing meta, forcing the model to emit confidence so that verify and redirect rewards can shape its behavior.\\\\n\\\\n**Hypothesis**: `confidence_omission_floor` (-0.5 for completions with no parseable meta block) will increase confidence coverage from 5.6% (E10) to >60%, while `same_route_repetition_penalty` and `route_switch_evidence_reward` improve execution quality. Overall accuracy should remain >= 38% (within 4.2 percentage points of base SFT 42.2%).\\\\n\\\\n**Mechanism**: Three new rewards are added on top of the E10 base:\\\\n1. `confidence_omission_floor`: Returns -0.5 when no meta block with parseable confidence exists, 0.0 otherwise. This makes omission costly without prescribing what confidence should be.\\\\n2. `same_route_repetition_penalty`: Same as E9v2. Penalizes decorative verify.\\\\n3. `route_switch_evidence_reward`: Same as E9bv2. Requires structural evidence for redirect.\\\\n\\\\n**Verification**:\\\\n- **Primary metric**: `confidence_coverage > 60%` AND `accuracy >= 38%`. Both must hold simultaneously.\\\\n- **Secondary metric**: Failure mode distribution shift. `no_meta_signal` should drop from 53/58 wrong answers (E10) to <10/58.\\\\n- **Falsification condition**: If accuracy drops below 30%, the combined reward pressure from 16 reward functions is too strong and non-correctness weights should be uniformly scaled by 0.5x.\\\\n\\\\n**Reward composition**:\\\\n\\\\n| Reward function | Weight | Source |\\\\n|---|---|---|\\\\n| correctness_reward | 3.0 | E10 |\\\\n| format_reward | 0.2 | E10 |\\\\n| correct_meta_reward | 0.3 | E10 |\\\\n| calibration_reward | 0.4 | E10 |\\\\n| confidence_revision_reward | 0.6 | E10 |\\\\n| overconfidence_penalty_reward | 1.0 | E10 |\\\\n| length_penalty_reward | 1.0 | E10 |\\\\n| effective_verification_reward | 0.8 | E10 |\\\\n| effective_redirection_reward | 1.0 | E10 (modified: tail check replaced) |\\\\n| diagnosis_reward | 0.6 | E10 |\\\\n| decomposition_reward | 0.6 | E10 |\\\\n| anomaly_notice_reward | 0.4 | E10 |\\\\n| repeated_intervention_reward | 0.5 | E10 |\\\\n| overconfidence_verify_reward | 1.0 | E10 |\\\\n| **same_route_repetition_penalty** | **0.5** | **NEW** |\\\\n| **route_switch_evidence_reward** | **0.6** | **NEW** |\\\\n| **confidence_omission_floor** | **0.5** | **NEW** |\\\\n\\\\n---\\\\n\\\\n## 4. New Reward Functions (Exact Specifications)\\\\n\\\\n### 4.1 `same_route_repetition_penalty`\\\\n\\\\n```python\\\\ndef same_route_repetition_penalty(completions, ground_truth=None, **kwargs):\\\\n    \\\\\\\"\\\\\\\"\\\\\\\"Penalize verification that restates the same derivation.\\\\n    \\\\n    Computes character trigram overlap between the pre-meta solve body\\\\n    and the post-meta solve tail. If overlap > 0.7, returns -1.0.\\\\n    If overlap 0.5-0.7, returns -0.3. Otherwise 0.0.\\\\n    Only fires when verify intent is detected in meta.\\\\n    \\\\\\\"\\\\\\\"\\\\\\\"\\\\n```\\\\n\\\\n| Condition | Reward |\\\\n|---|---|\\\\n| No verify intent in meta | 0.0 |\\\\n| Verify intent + trigram overlap > 0.7 | -1.0 |\\\\n| Verify intent + trigram overlap 0.5-0.7 | -0.3 |\\\\n| Verify intent + trigram overlap < 0.5 | 0.0 |\\\\n\\\\nWeight in E9v2: 0.5. Weight in E10v2: 0.5.\\\\n\\\\n### 4.2 `route_switch_evidence_reward`\\\\n\\\\n```python\\\\ndef route_switch_evidence_reward(completions, ground_truth=None, **kwargs):\\\\n    \\\\\\\"\\\\\\\"\\\\\\\"Reward structural method difference between pre-meta and post-meta.\\\\n    \\\\n    Extracts method keywords from pre-meta prefix and post-meta tail.\\\\n    Rewards genuine route switches; penalizes announced-but-not-executed switches.\\\\n    \\\\\\\"\\\\\\\"\\\\\\\"\\\\n```\\\\n\\\\n| Condition | Reward |\\\\n|---|---|\\\\n| No redirect signal in meta | 0.0 |\\\\n| Redirect signal + keyword Jaccard distance > 0.5 (genuine switch) + correct | +1.5 |\\\\n| Redirect signal + keyword Jaccard distance > 0.5 (genuine switch) + wrong | +0.3 |\\\\n| Redirect signal + keyword Jaccard distance < 0.2 (fake switch) | -0.5 |\\\\n| Redirect signal + keyword Jaccard distance 0.2-0.5 (ambiguous) | 0.0 |\\\\n\\\\nWeight in E9bv2: 0.6. RL 모델은 GRPO 학습 과정에서 correctness reward를 받기 위해 평가 함수가 인식하는 포맷으로 수렴한 반면, SFT 모델은 학습 데이터의 포맷을 그대로 재현했다. 이 발견은 두 가지를 시사한다. 첫째, 평가 파이프라인의 답안 파싱이 모델 비교의 공정성에 직접 영향을 미치므로, 포맷 정규화는 실험 설계의 필수 요소다. 둘째, format 수정 후에도 모든 Meta-CoT 모델이 base_sft를 하회하므로, 정확도 격차의 주원인은 포맷이 아니라 다른 곳에 있다.\nresults/study_metacot_v5_2026_04_05.md:186:Meta-CoT 모델의 응답을 meta 존재(present) / 부재(absent) 그룹으로 나누고, 각 그룹의 문제를 base_sft로 풀었을 때의 정확도를 비교한다. base_sft 정확도가 낮은 문제는 난이도가 높은 문제다. 두 그룹 간 base 정확도 격차는 선택 편향의 크기를 나타낸다.\nresults/study_metacot_v5_2026_04_05.md:192:**Table 2. 선택 편향 분석: meta 존재 문제와 부재 문제의 base_sft 정확도 비교**\nresults/study_metacot_v5_2026_04_05.md:202:H5는 기각된다. 모든 모델에서 meta가 존재하는 문제의 base_sft 정확도가 현저히 낮다. E8의 경우 격차가 -37.7pp에 달한다. 이는 모델이 어려운 문제에서 선택적으로 meta를 생성함을 의미한다.\nresults/study_metacot_v5_2026_04_05.md:298:| 지표 | base_sft | all_sft | 변화 |\nresults/study_metacot_v5_2026_04_05.md:308:| base_sft | 1 |\nresults/study_metacot_v5_2026_04_05.md:314:H4는 기각된다. Meta 블록은 completion 토큰의 15-25%를 소비하며, 이는 동일한 토큰 예산 내에서 본문 추론에 사용할 수 있는 토큰을 줄인다. E9c와 redirect_sft에서 각각 20건, 17건의 절단이 발생했다. 이는 base_sft의 1건에 비해 현저히 높다. 절단된 응답은 최종 답을 생성하지 못하므로 반드시 오답으로 처리된다.\nresults/study_metacot_v5_2026_04_05.md:316:토큰 오버헤드의 영향은 문제 난이도에 따라 비대칭적이다. GSM8K와 같은 쉬운 문제에서는 base_sft도 200-300 토큰으로 풀 수 있으므로 meta 오버헤드가 절단을 유발하지 않는다. 그러나 AIME이나 MATH-500의 어려운 문제에서는 풀이 자체가 2,000-3,000 토큰을 요구하므로, meta 블록의 추가 500-1,000 토큰이 절단을 유발할 수 있다. 역설적으로, meta가 가장 필요한 어려운 문제에서 meta의 토큰 비용이 가장 큰 부담이 된다.\nresults/study_metacot_v5_2026_04_05.md:340:(1) 정확도: 모든 RL 모델이 base_sft를 하회한다(Table 1). |\\nresults/codex_reviews/plan_review_1_log.txt:9:{\\\"type\\\":\\\"item.completed\\\",\\\"item\\\":{\\\"id\\\":\\\"item_3\\\",\\\"type\\\":\\\"command_execution\\\",\\\"command\\\":\\\"/bin/bash -lc \\\\\\\"sed -n '1,260p' results/experiment_plan_v5.md\\\\\\\"\\\",\\\"aggregated_output\\\":\\\"# Meta-CoT Experiment Plan v5: Fixing Meta Execution\\\\n\\\\n**Date**: 2026-04-04\\\\n**Author**: Seungpil Lee\\\\n**Project**: metacognition-math (Qwen3-8B)\\\\n**Predecessor**: experiment_plan_v4.md (accuracy-focused autoresearch loop)\\\\n\\\\n---\\\\n\\\\n## 1. Current State Summary\\\\n\\\\n### What works\\\\n\\\\n1. **Parseable meta**: The SFT-trained model emits well-formed `<|meta|>...<|/meta|>` blocks containing confidence, diagnosis, and strategy statements. Coverage reaches 88.9% on `all_sft`.\\\\n2. **Calibration (ECE reduction)**: E8 achieves ECE 0.322 with only 3.6% wrong-high-confidence, the best overconfidence suppression among all conditions.\\\\n3. **Overconfidence suppression (E8)**: `overconfidence_penalty_reward` + `confidence_revision_reward` successfully pushed wrong-high-conf from 80.7% (verify_sft) down to 3.6% (E8).\\\\n4. **Accuracy near parity (E9)**: E9 reaches 41.1% overall (base SFT: 42.2%), the closest Meta-CoT model to parity, driven by GSM8K 90.0%.\\\\n\\\\n### What does not work\\\\n\\\\n1. **Verify execution**: Verification is same-route repetition, not independent falsification. 15/53 wrong answers in E9 are overconfident-verify-failed: the model says \\\\\\\"verify\\\\\\\" then re-derives the same wrong answer (e.g., AIME 540 re-uses identical extremal intuition; GSM8K restart miscounts time identically).\\\\n2. **Redirect execution**: Diagnosis appears but the solve body continues the original route. 0/4 diagnosis cases in E10 led to actual recovery. `effective_redirection_reward` checks `bool(solve_tail.strip())` for recovery, so any non-empty tail passes regardless of whether it contains a route switch.\\\\n3. **Repeated intervention**: Hard problems get exactly one meta block. No ongoing controller loop is observed. The model treats meta as a one-shot annotation rather than an iterative self-monitor.\\\\n4. **Full controller (E10)**: Only 5.6% confidence coverage. 53 out of 58 wrong answers have no meta signal at all. The model learned to omit confidence to avoid calibration penalties.\\\\n\\\\n### Quantitative reference (n=90 pilot, 30 per benchmark)\\\\n\\\\n| Model | Acc | AIME | GSM8K | MATH500 | conf_cov | ECE | wrong_high_conf |\\\\n|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|\\\\n| base_sft | 42.2 | 13.3 | 80.0 | 33.3 | 0.0 | n/a | n/a |\\\\n| all_sft | 33.3 | 6.7 | 63.3 | 30.0 | 88.9 | 0.398 | 51.7 |\\\\n| E8 | 38.9 | 10.0 | 80.0 | 26.7 | 23.3 | 0.322 | 3.6 |\\\\n| E9 | 41.1 | 6.7 | 90.0 | 26.7 | 91.1 | 0.301 | 50.9 |\\\\n| E9b | 40.0 | 6.7 | 83.3 | 30.0 | 0.0 | n/a | n/a |\\\\n| E10 | 35.6 | 6.7 | 66.7 | 33.3 | 5.6 | 0.340 | 0.0 |\\\\n\\\\n---\\\\n\\\\n## 2. Root Cause Analysis\\\\n\\\\nThree code-level root causes explain why meta detection succeeds but meta execution fails.\\\\n\\\\n### Root Cause 1: `effective_verification_reward` rewards same-route repetition\\\\n\\\\n**Location**: `rewards.py` line 1016-1035, specifically `_has_effective_verification_signal` (line 119-125).\\\\n\\\\nThe function checks for word patterns (\\\\\\\"substitute\\\\\\\", \\\\\\\"plug back\\\\\\\", \\\\\\\"recalculat\\\\\\\") in the solve tail after the last meta block. The problem is that restating the same derivation with verification keywords counts as effective verification. There is no check for **structural independence** -- whether the verification method differs from the original solve route.\\\\n\\\\n**Consequence**: The model learns to append \\\\\\\"let me substitute back...\\\\\\\" followed by the same calculation. This gets rewarded at +0.8 for correct answers, reinforcing decorative verification.\\\\n\\\\n### Root Cause 2: `effective_redirection_reward` accepts any non-empty tail as recovery\\\\n\\\\n**Location**: `rewards.py` line 1038-1063, specifically line 1051: `has_tail_recovery = bool(solve_tail.strip())`.\\\\n\\\\nThe maximum reward (+1.0 for correct, +0.2 for wrong) requires `has_conflict and has_switch and has_drop and has_tail_recovery`. But `has_tail_recovery` is satisfied by any non-empty text after the last meta block -- including the original solve continuation that ignores the announced strategy switch.\\\\n\\\\n**Consequence**: The model announces \\\\\\\"switch to parity-based analysis\\\\\\\" in meta, then continues the original algebraic approach. Because the tail is non-empty, the redirection reward fires as if recovery occurred.\\\\n\\\\n### Root Cause 3: `calibration_reward` returns 0.0 for no meta, making omission cost-free\\\\n\\\\n**Location**: `rewards.py` line 656-710, specifically lines 679-680:\\\\n\\\\n```python\\\\nif not blocks or all(b[\\\\\\\"confidence\\\\\\\"] is None for b in blocks):\\\\n    rewards.append(0.0)\\\\n```\\\\n\\\\nWhen the model emits no meta blocks or omits confidence, it receives 0.0 from calibration. Meanwhile, emitting confidence on wrong answers risks negative reward from both the Brier component and the log scoring rule. Rational reward optimization therefore favors omitting confidence entirely.\\\\n\\\\n**Consequence**: E5 (conf_cov=1.1%), E9b (conf_cov=0.0%), and E10 (conf_cov=5.6%) all escaped calibration pressure by reducing meta emission. This makes calibration metrics uninterpretable and defeats the purpose of Meta-CoT.\\\\n\\\\n---\\\\n\\\\n## 3. Proposed Experiments\\\\n\\\\nAll three experiments start from the same SFT checkpoint: `qwen3_metacot_control_v5_all_sft`. This ensures the only variable is the reward composition.\\\\n\\\\n### E9v2: Verify Quality\\\\n\\\\n**Node**: EVAL (GPU 0-3, same as current eval lane)\\\\n\\\\n**Intent**: Teach the model that verification must use an independent method, not repeat the same calculation. The current verify reward conflates \\\\\\\"mentions verification keywords\\\\\\\" with \\\\\\\"actually performs a structurally different check.\\\\\\\"\\\\n\\\\n**Hypothesis**: Adding `same_route_repetition_penalty` (-0.5 when the solve tail after a verify announcement shares >70% n-gram overlap with the pre-meta solve body) will reduce `overconfident_verify_failed` rate from 15/53 (28.3%, E9) to <5/53 (9.4%) without reducing overall accuracy by more than 2 percentage points.\\\\n\\\\n**Mechanism**: The new penalty computes character trigram overlap between the pre-meta solve prefix and the post-meta solve tail. If overlap exceeds 70%, the verification is classified as same-route repetition. The existing `effective_verification_reward` remains unchanged -- the penalty is additive, creating a gradient between \\\\\\\"verify with a new method (+0.8)\\\\\\\" and \\\\\\\"verify by restating (-0.5).\\\\\\\"\\\\n\\\\n**Verification**:\\\\n- **Primary metric**: `overconfident_verify_failed` count on 1,030-problem eval. Target: <10% of wrong answers (currently 28.3%).\\\\n- **Secondary metric**: `independent_method_rate` = fraction of verify completions where trigram overlap <70%. Target: >50%.\\\\n- **Falsification condition**: If `wrong_high_conf` stays >40% despite the penalty, the trigram heuristic is too weak to detect repetition and a stronger structural check (e.g., operation-type extraction) is needed.\\\\n\\\\n**Reward composition**:\\\\n\\\\n| Reward function | Weight | Source |\\\\n|---|---|---|\\\\n| correctness_reward | 3.0 | E9 |\\\\n| format_reward | 0.2 | E9 |\\\\n| correct_meta_reward | 0.3 | E9 |\\\\n| calibration_reward | 0.4 | E9 |\\\\n| confidence_revision_reward | 0.6 | E9 |\\\\n| overconfidence_penalty_reward | 1.0 | E9 |\\\\n| length_penalty_reward | 1.0 | E9 |\\\\n| effective_verification_reward | 0.9 | E9 |\\\\n| overconfidence_verify_reward | 0.9 | E9 |\\\\n| **same_route_repetition_penalty** | **0.5** | **NEW** |\\\\n| **confidence_omission_floor** | **0.5** | **NEW** |\\\\n\\\\n---\\\\n\\\\n### E9bv2: Redirect Execution\\\\n\\\\n**Node**: TRAIN_B (GPU 0-3, dedicated training lane)\\\\n\\\\n**Intent**: Ensure that redirect rewards require structural evidence of a route switch in the solve body, not just a non-empty tail. The current reward fires whenever the model writes anything after announcing a redirect, even if that \\\\\\\"anything\\\\\\\" continues the original approach.\\\\n\\\\n**Hypothesis**: Replacing `bool(solve_tail.strip())` with `route_switch_evidence_reward` (+0.9 for structural method-keyword difference between pre-meta and post-meta, -0.3 for announced switch without evidence) will increase `diagnosis_with_recovery` rate from 0/4 (E10) to >50% on the AIME + MATH-hard slice.\\\\n\\\\n**Mechanism**: The new reward extracts method keywords (algebra, geometry, combinatorics, number theory, substitution, casework, induction, parity, modular, generating function, etc.) from (a) the pre-meta solve body and (b) the post-meta solve tail. If the two keyword sets overlap <50%, the redirect is classified as a genuine route switch. If they overlap >80% and the meta announced a switch, the penalty fires.\\\\n\\\\n**Verification**:\\\\n- **Primary metric**: `diagnosis_with_recovery / total_diagnosis` ratio on AIME (30) + MATH-hard (top-50 by difficulty) slice. Target: >50%.\\\\n- **Secondary metric**: Method keyword Jaccard distance between pre-meta prefix and post-meta tail. Target: mean distance >0.3 for redirect cases.\\\\n- **Falsification condition**: If models stop announcing redirects entirely (redirect_count drops from E9b's current level by >80%), the penalty weight is too harsh and should be reduced to 0.15.\\\\n\\\\n**Reward composition**:\\\\n\\\\n| Reward function | Weight | Source |\\\\n|---|---|---|\\\\n| correctness_reward | 3.0 | E9b |\\\\n| format_reward | 0.2 | E9b |\\\\n| correct_meta_reward | 0.3 | E9b |\\\\n| calibration_reward | 0.4 | E9b |\\\\n| confidence_revision_reward | 0.6 | E9b |\\\\n| overconfidence_penalty_reward | 1.0 | E9b |\\\\n| length_penalty_reward | 1.0 | E9b |\\\\n| effective_redirection_reward | 1.0 | E9b (modified: tail check replaced) |\\\\n| **route_switch_evidence_reward** | **0.6** | **NEW** |\\\\n| **confidence_omission_floor** | **0.5** | **NEW** |\\\\n\\\\n---\\\\n\\\\n### E10v2: Full Controller + Coverage Floor\\\\n\\\\n**Node**: E8 (GPU 0-3, dedicated training lane)\\\\n\\\\n**Intent**: Combine improved verify and redirect with mandatory meta emission. E10 failed because the model escaped calibration by omitting confidence. E10v2 adds a coverage floor that penalizes missing meta, forcing the model to emit confidence so that verify and redirect rewards can shape its behavior.\\\\n\\\\n**Hypothesis**: `confidence_omission_floor` (-0.5 for completions with no parseable meta block) will increase confidence coverage from 5.6% (E10) to >60%, while `same_route_repetition_penalty` and `route_switch_evidence_reward` improve execution quality. Overall accuracy should remain >= 38% (within 4.2 percentage points of base SFT 42.2%).\\\\n\\\\n**Mechanism**: Three new rewards are added on top of the E10 base:\\\\n1. `confidence_omission_floor`: Returns -0.5 when no meta block with parseable confidence exists, 0.0 otherwise. This makes omission costly without prescribing what confidence should be.\\\\n2. `same_route_repetition_penalty`: Same as E9v2. Penalizes decorative verify.\\\\n3. `route_switch_evidence_reward`: Same as E9bv2. Requires structural evidence for redirect.\\\\n\\\\n**Verification**:\\\\n- **Primary metric**: `confidence_coverage > 60%` AND `accuracy >= 38%`. Both must hold simultaneously.\\\\n- **Secondary metric**: Failure mode distribution shift. `no_meta_signal` should drop from 53/58 wrong answers (E10) to <10/58.\\\\n- **Falsification condition**: If accuracy drops below 30%, the combined reward pressure from 16 reward functions is too strong and non-correctness weights should be uniformly scaled by 0.5x.\\\\n\\\\n**Reward composition**:\\\\n\\\\n| Reward function | Weight | Source |\\\\n|---|---|---|\\\\n| correctness_reward | 3.0 | E10 |\\\\n| format_reward | 0.2 | E10 |\\\\n| correct_meta_reward | 0.3 | E10 |\\\\n| calibration_reward | 0.4 | E10 |\\\\n| confidence_revision_reward | 0.6 | E10 |\\\\n| overconfidence_penalty_reward | 1.0 | E10 |\\\\n| length_penalty_reward | 1.0 | E10 |\\\\n| effective_verification_reward | 0.8 | E10 |\\\\n| effective_redirection_reward | 1.0 | E10 (modified: tail check replaced) |\\\\n| diagnosis_reward | 0.6 | E10 |\\\\n| decomposition_reward | 0.6 | E10 |\\\\n| anomaly_notice_reward | 0.4 | E10 |\\\\n| repeated_intervention_reward | 0.5 | E10 |\\\\n| overconfidence_verify_reward | 1.0 | E10 |\\\\n| **same_route_repetition_penalty** | **0.5** | **NEW** |\\\\n| **route_switch_evidence_reward** | **0.6** | **NEW** |\\\\n| **confidence_omission_floor** | **0.5** | **NEW** |\\\\n\\\\n---\\\\n\\\\n## 4. New Reward Functions (Exact Specifications)\\\\n\\\\n### 4.1 `same_route_repetition_penalty`\\\\n\\\\n```python\\\\ndef same_route_repetition_penalty(completions, ground_truth=None, **kwargs):\\\\n    \\\\\\\"\\\\\\\"\\\\\\\"Penalize verification that restates the same derivation.\\\\n    \\\\n    Computes character trigram overlap between the pre-meta solve body\\\\n    and the post-meta solve tail. If overlap > 0.7, returns -1.0.\\\\n    If overlap 0.5-0.7, returns -0.3.
